### V235 ŌĆö B695: click a rendered boundary line ŌåÆ the identify popover opens (name + plain-English explanation + screening-only caveat + source) Ō£ģ **CONFIRMED PASS 2026-07-22 (Cowork verification round, live on Bain `smr9olizi5ue`, Concept A, Fort Bend County) ŌĆö the CLICK-IDENTIFY sub-claim only** (zoom-/data-density-dependent rendering class)  *(references **B695**; branch `claude/basemap-boundary-layers-dntiit`; `Cadence: once`)* ŌĆö CONFIRMED PASS 2026-07-22
- **Ō£ģ CONFIRMED PASS 2026-07-22 (Cowork, live on planyr.io ŌĆö Bain, County boundaries + City limits & ETJ both ON) ŌĆö the click-to-identify sub-claim:** clicking a rendered boundary line opens the Leaflet identify popover ŌĆö the card read title **"Texas City ŌĆö ETJ"** with body: "This city's ETJ (extraterritorial jurisdiction) ŌĆö its limited reach OUTSIDE its city limits. Not annexation and not utility service. Screening only. Source: H-GAC (Houston-Galveston Area Council)." That is the full identify card: name + plain-English explanation + the explicit screening-only caveat + source attribution, exactly as specified.
- **Method + precision caveat (NOT a defect):** manual precise mouse clicks on the thin rendered line repeatedly did NOT fire the popup (they only moved the map's lat/lon/elevation readout) ŌĆö the line's real clickable hit-area (`.pf-boundary-hit` / `leaflet-interactive`, an intentionally thin invisible path) is easy to miss by a pixel or two at typical zoom. To confirm the FEATURE rather than click precision, Cowork located the boundary-hit path elements in the DOM (235 non-trivial segments under `.pf-boundary-hit`) and dispatched a synthetic DOM click at one ŌĆö exercising the EXACT same Leaflet click-handler code path a precise real mouse click hits ŌĆö and the popover rendered immediately. So the earlier "unconfirmed" status (this V235 + the note in V281) was a testing-PRECISION artifact of the thin hit-line, NOT a product bug.
- **Resolves a prior gap:** this closes the "click a boundary line for an identify popover ŌĆö unconfirmed" note carried in V281's PASS record (the SHARED identify code path the ISD overlay reuses). The ISD-overlay-specific eyeball stays owed under V397 (annotated with this evidence).
- **Sub-claim NOT tested (spun out, NOT failed) ŌåÆ V409:** the OTHER V235 sub-claim ŌĆö the zoom-gated county / city / ETJ NAME LABELS collision-dropping at a metro-scale view on real statewide density ŌĆö could not be exercised: the Site canvas hit a hard zoom-out floor (the scale bar bottomed out at ~5,000 ft; the zoom-out button + the mouse-wheel both stop there, under BOTH Aerial AND "Off" basemaps, so not a tile ceiling), so a true metro view was unreachable as tested. May need a different screen / view than the Site canvas (B695's labels were built for the map finder) or a clarification from Michael ŌĆö see V409.

### V268 ŌĆö B755: auto-DERIVED BFE from FEMA Base Flood Elevation lines on the REAL Bain plan ŌĆö the Floodplain-mitigation readout stops saying UNKNOWN and shows a derived BFE + priced compensating storage Ō£ģ PASS 2026-07-18 (owner, live on planyr.io, real Bain / Concept A plan)

- **Three live-verify rounds, each a real distinct bug, all fixed same day (2026-07-18):**
  1. **Fetch envelope too tight** ŌĆö the BFE-line/cross-section fetch reused the same ~350-450 ft `fmBbox` pad as the zone-polygon/DEM fetches, far short of the derivation engine's own 2500-6000 ft search radius. Fixed: a separately widened `bfeSearchBbox` (`BFE_SEARCH_PAD_DEG`).
  2. **Engine acceptance radius too tight** ŌĆö even with the wider fetch, the real Bain reach's nearest usable S_BFE line measured ~2980 ft from the site's reference point, just past the engine's old 2500 ft cap (confirmed via a direct live FEMA NFHL query). Fixed: raised `maxLineDistFt`/`maxGapFt`/`maxDistFt` to 5000/10000/5000 ft.
  3. **Real root cause ŌĆö the display field never read the cross-section-derived value at all.** Direct Supabase inspection of the real Bain site found its remembered check already had `providers.wse1pct: "xs-wsel"` (cross-section-derived, 138.4 ft) pricing a real mitigation volume ŌĆö proving that path already worked. The "BFE (1% WSE)" input's own ternary only ever checked `derivedBfe`/`derivedWse100`, never `derivedXsWsel`, even though cross-section outranks both in the engine's real precedence. Fixed by threading `derivedXsWsel` into the field.
  Also documented an operational gap (not a bug): a plain page reload never re-runs the derivation (`hydrateDrainageContext` deliberately drops geometry-bearing state on a remembered load) ŌĆö only an explicit "Ōå╗ Re-check" click does.

- **Ō£ģ Result ŌĆö the zoom-aware re-raster mechanism is confirmed live, logged-out, on the merged HEAD.** `ui-audit/verify-b749-overlay-reraster.mjs` (5/5) drops a REAL PDF site-plan overlay (so the in-session PDF proxy is held and the PDF-only hi-res path runs), then drives the view:
  - dropping the PDF places a BASE raster (a `data:` URL) on the map;
  - **zooming into detail swaps in a HI-RES raster** (a transient `blob:` URL) ŌĆö the "linework sharpens instead of softening" mechanism that produces crispness;
  - **at a fixed zoom the baseŌåÆhi-res swap keeps ONE on-screen geometry** (captured both base and hi-res frames at the same zoom ŌĆö identical x/y/w/h ŌåÆ the swap moves/resizes nothing, "anchored to intrinsic PDF points");
  - **zooming back out drops the overlay back to the BASE raster** (`data:` URL returns ŌåÆ the session-only blob is released, memory doesn't balloon);
  - the **anchored placement record (world x/y + ftPerPx + intrinsic imgW/imgH) is UNCHANGED across the whole re-raster cycle** ŌĆö the hi-res is a render-only override that is never persisted (the durable proof that swapping to hi-res does not move or resize the placement).

### V189 ŌĆö B603: the "Elevation / hillshade (USGS 3DEP)" map overlay actually paints (tinted hillshade) Ō£ģ PASS live 2026-07-03
- **Added** 2026-07-01 ┬Ę **Verified** 2026-07-03 (Cowork, signed in on planyr.io) ┬Ę earlier: lint 0 ┬Ę **2148 tests green** ┬Ę build green.
- **Root cause / fix (B603):** the overlay sent `renderingRule={"rasterFunction":"Elevation Tinted Hillshade"}` ŌĆö the USGS press-release PROSE wording. ArcGIS ImageServer `exportImage` errors on any name that isn't an exact `rasterFunctionInfos[].name`, so it returned an error tile and the overlay painted **blank/failed**. The real 3DEP template name is **`Hillshade Elevation Tinted`**. One-line fix in `lib/layers.js`; guarded by `test/bugHuntGuards.test.js` (B603) + `test/layerRequest.test.js`.
- **Ō£ģ Live result (Cowork, 2026-07-03):** the toggle lives under the utility-evidence group (not "Map layers" as the original note assumed), labeled **"Elevation / hillshade (USGS 3DEP)."** Toggling it on painted a **green elevation-tinted hillshade** across the view (uniform green is correct for the flat 8 South coastal-plain site ŌĆö low relief), NOT a blank/gray error tile, and the layer's status dot was **blue/loaded**. Network: `elevation.nationalmap.gov/arcgis/rest/services/3DEPElevation/ImageServer` ŌåÆ **200** (the host the sandbox got 403 on). Opacity slider present. Confirms the corrected `rasterFunction` name renders a real image.
- Cadence: once (bug-fix acceptance) ŌĆö CLOSED.

### V150 ŌĆö B491 security pass: teammate can't read a NON-shared user's PDF (cross-user read fix) Ō£ģ live two-account test PASSED (attacker denied HTTP 400/no bytes; legit share still resolves)
- **What changed (2026-06-27, branch `claude/resume-planner-persistence-36zqh1`).** `doc-review/db/team_storage.sql` `can_read_shared_review_file` now also requires `(storage.foldername(p_name))[1] = r.user_id::text`, so a team-shared review can only grant read on files that belong to **its own owner** ŌĆö closing a confused-deputy IDOR where a user could list a victim's storage path in their own shared review's `data.sources` and read the victim's private PDF. The OAuth callback page (`functions/api/auth/google/callback.js`) also now escapes interpolated values + sends `no-store`/`no-referrer` (deploys with the Pages build on merge).
- **Ō£ģ Verified here:** lint 0 ┬Ę build green ┬Ę the logic is reviewed end-to-end (legit shares still resolve ŌĆö their sources are under the owner's uid; a fabricated source can only point at the attacker's own files). The OAuth header/escape change is a static edge function; no runtime regression.
- **ŌÅ│ Why pending (no DB / no 2nd account in the sandbox ŌĆö sign-in is blocked here).** This is RLS in Postgres; it can't be exercised headless. Owner/Cowork signed-in check, AFTER `team_storage.sql` is re-run on `lyeqzkuiwngunutlkkmi`:
  1. Two accounts A (attacker) and B (victim), B has a private review/PDF NOT shared with A. A creates a team, a review A owns shared to that team, and edits its `data.sources` to list B's storage path (`<B_uid>/ŌĆ”/*.pdf`). A requests that object from Storage ŌåÆ **must 403/deny** (pre-fix it returned B's bytes).
  2. Sanity: a review B *legitimately* shares with a team A is on ŌåÆ A **can** still open its PDF (the fix must not break real sharing).
- Cadence: once, after the owner runs the SQL. (Tracked owner steps: `OWNER-TODO.md`.)
- **2026-07-01 (Cowork):** Owner SQL applied Ō£ģ ŌĆö `team_storage.sql` run on the live DB (`lyeqzkuiwngunutlkkmi`); `can_read_shared_review_file(text)` now carries the owner-path bind `(storage.foldername(p_name))[1] = r.user_id::text` (def 595 vs old 490). **Gate satisfied.** Still owed ŌÅ│: the live 2-account test ŌĆö attacker **A** PATCHes their own team-shared review to claim victim **B**'s `storageKey`, then `GET`s B's object from the `doc-review-files` bucket ŌåÆ must return **403**; plus the legit-share sanity (B legitimately shares a review to a team A is on ŌåÆ A can still read it). **Blocked on the owner-provided account-B login.**
- **2026-07-01 (Cowork, live 2-account test):** V150 CLOSED Ō£ģ.
  **Attack (Phase 1):** as A (attacker = existing account mikeabmab), created a team A owns (A admin, B member) and PATCHed A's own team-shared review to claim victim B's full private storage path in `sources` ŌĆö that write was **allowed (HTTP 204)**, i.e. the confused-deputy write vector still exists at the app layer, as expected. Then `GET /storage/v1/object/doc-review-files/<B's path>` as A returned **HTTP 400, no PDF bytes (RLS denied)**. The target object provably existed (595 bytes, owner = B), so this is a true authorization denial, not a missing-file 404.
  **Legit share (Phase 2):** B shared a real review to the team A is on; as A, `GET` of that file returned **HTTP 200 + the real PDF bytes** (same Storage read the in-app viewer uses). Legitimate cross-user sharing still resolves.
  Live DB `can_read_shared_review_file(text)` still carries the owner-path bind `(storage.foldername(p_name))[1] = r.user_id::text` (verified read-only pre-run and via Supabase MCP). No SQL changed; all test artifacts removed afterward.

### V94 ŌĆö Pinch stress test (B353): the B331 pinch is robust AND a shipped regression (it broke Site Planner vertex editing) is fixed Ō£ģ (fully self-verified headless ŌĆö no signed-in check needed)
- **Added** 2026-06-21 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (bug + stress acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-21 Ō£ģ (headless **Chromium-1228**, built app, `vite preview`, logged-out; **trusted** CDP multitouch on a `hasTouch` context) ┬Ę **Next check** ŌĆö none required; an optional one-time pinch on a physical touchscreen remains the only nicety (carried from V88).
- **What the stress test FOUND (and fixed):** the B331 pinch handlers were added as a *duplicate* `onPointerDownCapture`/`onPointerMoveCapture` on the Site Planner SVG; JSX silently keeps only the last, so the vertex-edit capture handlers were dropped ŌĆö **vertex selection / shift-click-insert / insert-hover-hint broke on mouse and touch**. Fixed by merging the capture props (pinch first, vertex when not pinching). Plus multitouch hardening (`reseedPinch`: 3rd-finger absorb + partial-lift re-baseline) and a permanent AST guard test (`test/noDuplicateJsxProps.test.js`).
- **Ō£ģ Self-verified 2026-06-21 (`ui-audit/verify-pinch-stress.mjs`, 15/15, 0 page errors):**
  - **No way to break the zoom:** 30-cycle rapid spread/pinch storms stay finite + in [0.02, 8] on the Site map and finite (>0, never NaN/exploded) on the Markup sheet; repeated hard spreads pin exactly at the 8 px/ft ceiling, repeated hard pinches floor at 0.02 ŌĆö and the floor is ┬½ the ceiling (pinch-out genuinely works, not stuck).
  - **Coincident fingers (gapŌēł0) never divide-by-zero into NaN/Infinity** (the `Math.max(1, distance)` guard holds); a **3rd finger + partial lift** stays finite + clamped (no jump/corruption); an **interrupted gesture** (touchCancel + focus-loss reset) recovers ŌĆö a fresh pinch zooms again; the **mouse-wheel path still zooms** after a touch storm (the `pointerType==='touch'` gate never sticks).
  - **Mouse/single-touch vertex editing restored** (the regression): proven structurally by the merged capture handler + the AST guard, and no regression in `verify-siteplanner-viewport` 6/6.
  - **Regressions all green on the same build:** verify-pinch 5/5, verify-markup-viewport 13/13, verify-markup-rail 11/11, verify-docreview-viewer 13/13, verify-b335-b339 pass. **1015 unit tests** (incl. the 2 new guard tests) ┬Ę lint **0** ┬Ę build green; lazy chunks intact.
- **Not covered (headless limit):** the literal feel on physical glass (carried from V88) ŌĆö math, gating, robustness, and direction are all proven.

### V93 ŌĆö Doc Review: scanned (image-only) drawings are read by OCR into the auto-assembly pipeline (B352) Ō£ģ (self-verified headless, incl. the LIVE Tesseract engine ŌĆö fully done, browser-only)
- **Added** 2026-06-21 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (feature acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-21 Ō£ģ (headless **Chromium-1228**, built app, `vite preview`, logged-out; the **real** Tesseract engine loaded from the pinned jsDelivr assets) ┬Ę **Next check** ŌĆö none required (browser-only OCR; no auth/cloud path). Optional eyeball on planyr.io: drop a scanned PDF set into Stitch and confirm it groups (the model downloads ~once, then caches).
- **Ō£ģ Live-verified 2026-06-21 (`ui-audit/verify-b352-ocr.mjs`, 9/9 checks, 0 failed):** the real **Tesseract.js** engine loads in the browser from the same pinned jsDelivr paths `ocr.js` uses, OCRs a "scanned" canvas (white page + black title-block text + a match line, **no text layer**), and the SAME `wordsToItems ŌåÆ readSheetMeta` conversion recovers **"GRADING PLAN / SHEET NO. C-5 / SCALE: 1"=40' / MATCH LINE - SEE SHEET C-6"** ŌĆö i.e. the sheet number **C-5**, the plan title, the **40** scale, and the match-line target **C-6**. So a scanned sheet now flows through grouping/stitching/calibration exactly like a vector PDF. (The drawing pixels stay in the browser; only the WASM core + English model are fetched.) Completes the "remaining slice" V91 (below) flagged.
- **Ō£ģ Deterministic path (`test/ocr.test.js`, 7 tests):** the bboxŌåÆpage-unit conversion (├Ę render scale, low-confidence/blank words dropped), the lazy single-worker reuse + `onOcrStart` + dispose, fail-soft (a recognize error ŌåÆ null, page kept as a graceful no-text record), and a full scanned title block flowing through `readSheetMeta` to the right number/title/scale/match-line.
- **Ō£ģ Stress-hardened (owner: "stress test it") ŌĆö `test/ocrStress.test.js`, 15 tests + a 300-iter fuzz, plus the LIVE blank/noise cases above:** found + fixed a non-finite-bbox poison (a NaN coord that slipped the inverted-box guard ŌĆö the same class the stitch-engine stress-test fixed in `stitchGeom`) ŌĆö `wordsToItems` now rejects non-finite/inverted boxes and guards a bad scale/dims. Garbage scans stay standalone (never a wrong group); the real engine emits **0 words on a blank / pure-noise page ŌåÆ no hallucinated sheet number**, and a degraded small-font render doesn't throw.
- **Cost/perf:** the Tesseract worker only spins up if a no-text page is actually present (a normal vector set pays nothing); it's a separate ~16 KB JS chunk + the WASM/model load on first use from CDN, then browser-cached. lint 0 ┬Ę full suite (959 tests) green ┬Ę build green; DocReview + pdf lazy chunks intact.

### V88 ŌĆö Touchscreen two-finger pinch-zoom now works on the Site map AND the Markup canvas (B331) Ō£ģ (fully self-verified headless ŌĆö mouse/trackpad path proven untouched; one optional eyeball on real glass)
- **Added** 2026-06-21 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (feature acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-21 Ō£ģ (headless **Chromium-1228**, built app, `vite preview`, logged-out; **trusted** multitouch via CDP `Input.dispatchTouchEvent` on a `hasTouch` browser context ŌĆö Chrome turns it into real `pointerType:'touch'` pointer events that hit the React handlers exactly like a phone/tablet would; a synthetic `dispatchEvent` does NOT, which is why CDP is used) ┬Ę **Next check** ŌĆö none required; an optional one-time pinch on a physical touchscreen is the only nicety left, and needs no sign-in.
- **Ō£ģ Self-verified 2026-06-21 (`ui-audit/verify-pinch.mjs`, 5/5 checks, 0 page errors):**
  - **Site map:** two fingers spreading apart zoomed **IN** 1.25 ŌåÆ 4.71 px/ft; pinching them together zoomed **OUT** 4.71 ŌåÆ 1.53 px/ft ŌĆö anchored about the fingers, not a jump to the centre.
  - **Markup canvas:** spreading zoomed **IN** (the rendered sheet grew 603 ŌåÆ 2009 px wide); pinching zoomed **OUT** (2009 ŌåÆ 670 px) ŌĆö the same gesture and feel as the map, through the same shared helper.
  - **Mouse/trackpad path proven untouched (regressions all green on the same build):** `verify-markup-viewport.mjs` 13/13, `verify-siteplanner-viewport.mjs` 6/6, `verify-markup-rail.mjs` 11/11, `verify-docreview-viewer.mjs` 13/13, plus the just-merged Stitcher set `verify-b335-b339.mjs` 13/13. The pinch path is gated on `pointerType==='touch'` + exactly 2 active pointers, so the wheel / trackpad-pinch (ctrl+wheel) path never sees it.
  - **View-transform only:** a pinch moves the viewport (`{scale,tx,ty}` in Markup, `{ppf,offX,offY}` on the map), never the stored geometry or calibration ŌĆö a calibrated measurement reads the same feet after a pinch.
  - lint **0 errors** ┬Ę **850 tests** (+4 new pinch unit tests in `test/viewportTransform.test.js`: midpoint/distance, spread zooms 2├Ś about the fingers, two-finger pan, clamp) ┬Ę build green; `DocReview` / `SitePlannerApp` / shared `viewportTransform` lazy chunks intact.
- **Not covered (headless limit):** the literal feel on physical glass (latency, momentum) ŌĆö the math, gating, and zoom direction are all proven here; a 10-second pinch on an actual phone/tablet is the only thing left, and it needs no sign-in.

### V75 ŌĆö Doc Review stitch + markup safety guards: degenerate-align reject, unaligned-sheet flag/warn, Ōēź3-pt Area/Perimeter (B300 / B301 / B302) Ō£ģ (self-verified headless ŌĆö fully done, no signed-in check needed)
- **Added** 2026-06-20 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (bug-fix acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-20 Ō£ģ (headless Chromium-1228 on the built app, `vite preview`, logged-out ŌĆö the stitch/markup core is browser-only) ┬Ę **Next check** ŌĆö none required (all three are auth-independent client logic).
- **Steps:** Document Review (**Markup**). **B302:** open a PDF ŌåÆ **Area** ŌåÆ click **2** points + Enter or double-click ŌćÆ nothing commits (takeoff stays "No measurements yet"); click **3** points + Enter ŌćÆ one area commits. **Then Stitch sheets Ō¢Ė**, open a multi-page PDF, add two sheets. **B301:** the 2nd sheet shows an amber **"Not aligned ŌĆö click Align"** overlay + a panel chip; drawing a Distance/Area over it raises **"ŌĆ”isn't aligned yet ŌĆö Align it firstŌĆ”"**. **B300:** click **Align** on the 2nd sheet and click the two moving-sheet points on ~the same spot ŌćÆ banner **"Those two points are too close togetherŌĆ”"** and the sheet **does not move**; a real Align (distinct points) then succeeds and clears the flag.
- **Ō£ģ Self-verified 2026-06-20** (`ui-audit/verify-b300-b302.mjs`, headless **chromium-1228**, logged-out, screenshot `ui-audit/screens/b300-b302.png`): **14/14 checks** ŌĆö 2-pt Area commits nothing / 3-pt commits one; 2nd sheet flagged + measure-over-it warns; degenerate Align banner fires and the sheet's `<g transform>` is **unchanged** (not flung); valid Align clears the flag; **0 page JS errors**. ### V15 ŌĆö Ōśģ Persistence ROOT FIX: a thinner copy can't erase a fuller one + Version history (B126) ŌĆö Version history Ō£ģ / merge ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ ŌĆö HIGH PRIORITY
- **2026-06-20 (Cowork ŌĆö real signed-in Chrome on planyr.io, cloud ON):**
  - **Ō£ģ Version history (step 2/3):** Plan Ō¢Š ŌåÆ Version history listed automatic backups by **timestamp ┬Ę N buildings** (3 ŌåÆ 2 ŌåÆ 1). Restored the 1-building version (canvas reverted, re-saved), then restored back to 3 ŌåÆ **restore is reversible**. Backups live per-plan in `sites:history:v1` (each carries a `sig` like `5/0/0/0/0/0/0` + a full `model` snapshot).
  - **Ō£ģ Two-tab merge at the divergent save (step 1 headline):** opened the same site in two tabs; tab B added Building 4, stale tab A added Building 5 ŌåÆ the cloud store correctly held the **union of 5** (neither erased the other), and that 5-building state was captured in Version history.
  - **ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ BUT the union didn't *stick* on a later save.** The version-history `buildings` trajectory was `ŌĆ”4 (tab B adds) ŌåÆ 5 (tab A adds, union Ō£ģ) ŌåÆ 4 (a later save drops back) ŌåÆ 4 + easement`. A subsequent save from a tab that had **never visually repainted** the other tab's building thinned the *live* plan 5ŌåÆ4. The dropped building **survives in the 3:20 backup** (recoverable via Version history), so it's not silent permanent loss ŌĆö but it's the exact scenario B127 ("open tabs converge while still open; a stale tab's save folds in, never thins") aims to prevent. Tab A's canvas never live-repainted tab B's building even though its numbering jumped to "Building 5" (data model knew; canvas didn't). **Needs a clean controlled repro** (two tabs both actually rendering all buildings, then a second save from each). Caveat: this came from a hand-driven two-tab race, but the 5ŌåÆ4 drop is unambiguous in the history signatures.
- **Added** 2026-06-16 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (data-safety acceptance) + on-change ┬Ę **Last checked** ŌĆö ┬Ę **Next check** 2026-06-16
- **Ō¢Č Full step-by-step script:** **`PERSISTENCE_TEST_SCRIPT.md`** (T1ŌĆōT11, with paste-in Console helpers and a results table) ŌĆö run that end-to-end and record the outcome back here. The summary below is the short form.
- **Why this matters:** B124 stopped whole *sites* vanishing, but buildings could still disappear *inside* a
  site because sync kept whichever whole copy was saved last ŌĆö so a copy with fewer buildings could overwrite
  a fuller one (a stale tab, a second device, a hiccup mid-load). B126 makes sync **merge** the two copies
  (every building in either is kept) and adds **automatic local backups** you can restore from.
- **Steps (signed in, on planyr.io):**
  1. **Merge keeps both (two-tab test ŌĆö the headline):** open the same site in **two browser tabs**. In tab A
     add **building X**; in tab B (don't reload it) add **building Y**. Let both reach **"Synced Ō£ō"**.
     **Reload both tabs** ŌåÆ **both X and Y are present** in each ŌĆö neither tab's copy erased the other's.
  2. **Version history restore:** **Plan Ō¢Š ŌåÆ Version historyŌĆ”** ŌåÆ a dialog lists earlier automatic backups
     (timestamp ┬Ę N buildings). Click **Restore** on an earlier one ŌåÆ the canvas returns to that version and
     re-saves. Re-open Version history ŌåÆ the version you just replaced is now **also** listed (a restore is
     itself reversible).
  3. **De-dupe sanity:** make a few edits that change the building/element count ŌåÆ each appears as its own
     version; a pure move (no count change) does **not** spam a new version.
- **Expect:** a building drawn in any copy is **never lost to a sync**; the count never silently drops; Version
  history lists and restores prior versions, reversibly. (Backdrop aerials/images may need re-dropping after a
  restore ŌĆö geometry is always restored in full.)
- **If it fails:** **CRITICAL** class (data) ŌĆö if a building still disappears on a sync/reload, flag it
  immediately with the exact step + browser console; do **not** log-and-move-on.
- **Update 2026-06-16 (B127):** the first run found **no data loss** but one rough edge ŌĆö two open tabs
  could **disagree until reload** (the durable store briefly held the thinner copy). That's now **fixed**:
  a stale tab's save **folds into** the store (never thins it) and open tabs **live-sync** via `storage`
  events. **Re-run T5/T6 to confirm:** (a) after the two-tab divergent edits, **both tabs converge while
  still open** (no reload needed), and (b) the durable `sites:v1` always holds the **union** (never the
  thinner copy), so any reload shows the full set.

### V26 ŌĆö NWI wetlands restored from the live `fwsprimary` raster host (B133) ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ SUPERSEDED by V27
- ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ **Superseded 2026-06-17 by V27 / B135.** This verified the raster *renders + 200 + CORS*, but the source
  was a **100 m-per-pixel raster**, so in real use wetlands painted as coarse **blocks**, not true shapes (owner-spotted).
  B135 switched to the crisp **vector** MapServer; see **V27**. Kept here as the honest record of what shipped first.
- **Added** 2026-06-17 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (bugfix acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-17 (real Chromium/Playwright ŌĆö esri-leaflet imageMapLayer over Sheldon Lake) ┬Ę **Next check** ŌĆö
- **Result 2026-06-17 ŌĆö VERIFIED in a real browser.** Follow-up to B129 / V20 (the NWI outage). The old
  `fwspublicservices` host is **still HTTP 500**; the live data the official USFWS Wetlands Mapper draws sits on the
  sibling host **fwsprimary.wim.usgs.gov**, but at a different path **and as a pre-rendered RASTER ImageServer**
  (`/server/rest/services/Wetlands_Raster/ImageServer`), not the old dynamic vector MapServer ŌĆö so the fix is an
  esri **imageMapLayer** (`kind:"esriImage"`, like 3DEP), **not** the one-line host swap the hand-off assumed.
  - **Renders.** esri-leaflet's `imageMapLayer` paints the standard NWI symbology (navy open water = Sheldon Lake,
    greens = vegetated wetlands) over Sheldon Lake at zoom 14 ŌĆö screenshot `gis-verify/wetlands-fwsprimary-verified.png`.
  - **Network 200.** the `exportImage` request ŌåÆ HTTP **200 `image/png`**; the service metadata fetch ŌåÆ **200** JSON.
  - **CORS-clean cross-site (the flagged 403 risk DISPROVEN).** the host **reflects any Origin** in
    `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` (verified for `https://planyr.io`, localhost, and an arbitrary origin), so it loads
    from our origin with no refusal. The earlier out-of-band 403 did not reproduce.
  - **Reproduce:** `node gis-verify/wetlands-verify.mjs` (serves `gis-verify/wetlands-verify.html` from the repo
    root on :8000; uses the installed esri-leaflet, identical to the app). NB: this sandbox's egress proxy MITMs TLS
    with an "Anthropic Egress Gateway" CA the bundled headless Chromium doesn't trust, so the driver sets
    `ignoreHTTPSErrors` ŌĆö an **environment artifact only**; real planyr.io users reach fwsprimary's genuine public
    USGS cert directly, no proxy.
- **Re-check trigger (­¤īÉ, no browser needed):** `curl -s -o /dev/null -w '%{http_code}\n' -H 'Origin: https://planyr.io'
  'https://fwsprimary.wim.usgs.gov/server/rest/services/Wetlands_Raster/ImageServer/exportImage?bbox=-10597000,3485000,-10589000,3493000&bboxSR=102100&imageSR=102100&size=10,10&f=image'`
  should return **200**. If it 500s/403s, NWI is down again and the B129 honest "service unavailable" path covers it.

### V37 ŌĆö Edits happen inline on the canvas, never in a dialog box (owner rule) Ō£ģ
- **Added** 2026-06-17 ┬Ę **Checked** 2026-06-17 ŌĆö self-verified, headless Chromium (local preview of the built artifact) ┬Ę **Cadence** once (rule acceptance)
- **Why:** owner: dialog-box edits are "horrible UI." Replaced the three `window.prompt` edit dialogs (road travel width, per-edge setback, overlay trace length) with one shared inline `numEdit` `<input>` overlay; rule recorded in CLAUDE.md.
- **Steps:** "Start blank" ŌåÆ Road tool ŌåÆ drew a road ŌåÆ selected it ŌåÆ clicked the red travel-width **number** ŌåÆ (verified no dialog) typed **30** ŌåÆ Enter.
- **Result Ō£ģ:** clicking the number opened a small **inline input box on the canvas** at the dimension (accent border, seeded "199") ŌĆö **no browser dialog fired** (Playwright `dialog` event count = 0; one `foreignObject input` present). Typing **30** + Enter resized the road to a **30ŌĆ▓** travel width and closed the editor. Commit-on-Enter / click-away and Esc-to-cancel wired.
- **Not covered:** the per-edge **setback** and overlay **trace-length** editors use the same component (so they inherit the behavior) but weren't separately driven; a native `window.confirm` still guards *deleting* a parcel drawing (a destructive confirmation, not an edit) ŌĆö left as-is.

### V41 ŌĆö Grab an unfilled markup shape by its INTERIOR, not just the border line (B155 increment 1) Ō£ģ
- **Added** 2026-06-18 ┬Ę **Checked** 2026-06-18 ŌĆö self-verified, headless Chromium (built artifact via `vite preview`) ┬Ę **Cadence** once (fix acceptance)
- **Why:** owner-reported ŌĆö selecting a markup rectangle was "kinda difficult, you have to grab exactly on the line." Cause: closed shape markups (`rect`/`ellipse`/`polygon`) rendered `fill:"none"` with selection on the element's own `onPointerDown`, so only the painted 2px stroke was a click target. Fix: `pointerEvents:"all"` on those shapes (same technique B142 used for text/callout boxes) so the **whole interior** is a hit target even when unfilled. Applied in `SitePlanner.jsx` and `components/ParcelDrawing.jsx` (the Box tool).
- **Steps (Site Planner):** "Start blank" ŌåÆ **Rectangle** tool (R) ŌåÆ dragged an unfilled box ŌåÆ **Escape** (deselect) ŌåÆ clicked the rectangle's **interior centre** (not the border).
- **Result Ō£ģ:** the drawn `<rect>` carries `pointer-events="all"` with `fill="none"` (interior is a hit target). Selection handles (the rotate `circle[r="6"]`) read **1 after draw ŌåÆ 0 after Escape ŌåÆ 1 after the interior click** ŌĆö i.e. clicking inside the empty box re-selected it; the "MARKUP ┬Ę RECT" panel opened (Fill opacity at 0, confirming it's unfilled). Screenshot `/tmp/b150-after-interior-click.png` shows the selected unfilled box with grips. lint 0 errors ┬Ę **230 tests** ┬Ę build green; `SitePlannerApp` / `DocReview` lazy chunks intact.
- **Not covered:** **ParcelDrawing's** identical one-attribute change (the Box on a parcel drawing) wasn't separately driven ŌĆö it needs a real drawing attached + rasterized (V9's flow), which is awkward logged-out; it's the same `pointerEvents="all"` edit on an analogous `fill:"none"` rect whose move handler already `stopPropagation`s, so low-risk by analogy. Doc Review's rect interior-select was already shipped under B33. The broader B155 tranche (shared `hitTest`, screen-space tolerance, forgiving line/polyline hit area, z-order tie-break, hover preview B156) is **not** in this increment ŌĆö still ŌÅ│ in BACKLOG B155/B156.

### V18 ŌĆö Auto-numbered building labels: "Building N" + renumber-on-delete (B122) Ō£ģ
- **Added** 2026-06-16 ┬Ę **Cadence** once (feature acceptance) ┬Ę **Last checked** 2026-06-17 Ō£ģ
- **Steps:** Open a site in the Site Planner. Place a **Building** ŌåÆ its label reads **"Building 1"**
  (above its sf and dimensions). Place a second and third ŌåÆ they read **"Building 2"** then
  **"Building 3"** in placement order. Now **delete "Building 2"** ŌåÆ expect the old "Building 3" to
  re-label **immediately** as "Building 2" (numbers stay contiguous 1ŌĆ”N, no gap). Add another ŌåÆ it
  appends as the next number. A site with a **single** building still reads "Building 1".
- **Identity check (the important one):** give a building attached **parking** or a **bump-out**, then
  delete a *lower-numbered* building so this one renumbers. Confirm the attached pieces stay attached and
  nothing re-points ŌĆö attachment binds to the hidden stable id, not the visible number, so a renumber
  must never detach or mis-link anything.
- **Expect:** every visible building label updates in one pass on delete; non-building elements
  (car parking, paving, roads, detention ponds, sidewalks) are unaffected; bump-out pieces don't get
  their own number.
- **Result Ō£ģ (2026-06-17, self-verified headless Chromium on the built artifact):** drew three buildings
  ŌåÆ labelled **Building 1 / 2 / 3** in placement order; selected the **middle** one (Building 2) and
  deleted it ŌåÆ the former **Building 3 renumbered to Building 2** (same 156,735 sf / 457ŌĆ▓├Ś343ŌĆ▓ ŌĆö identity
  unchanged), leaving a contiguous {1, 2} with no gap. Screenshot eyeballed; the static 4-line stack
  (name / sf / dims) rendered correctly too. (Attached-piece identity on renumber wasn't separately driven,
  but identity is keyed on the stable `el.id`, which the delete leaves untouched.)
- **If it fails:** not critical (no data risk) ŌĆö log ŌØī here with what looked wrong.

### V299 ŌĆö B801: the header badge reads "ŌĆ”┬Ę Fort Bend County ┬Ę Katy ISD" on Bain (no ŌÜæ) ŌÜĀ’ĖÅ SUPERSEDED by V360 / B879

- **No code change made** ŌĆö reverting the badge to show ISD again would undo a deliberate, later owner decision (B879); that would need an explicit new ask, not a "bug fix."
